## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear dynamics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator expressed in state-space variables (x, v) and possibly explicit time forcing (t). Common models combine a restoring force f(x), damping/drive terms g(v) or g(x,v), and periodic/parametric excitation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear spring, no damping/drive)
- Viscously damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear restoring from geometry)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * Abs(v) * v (mixed linear + quadratic damping)
- Liénard-type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (damping depends on displacement amplitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v - c2 * x (nonlinear damping in v leading to oscillations)
- Parametrically excited (Mathieu-type) oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) + c5 * cos(c6 * t) (combined nonlinear stiffness and multi-harmonic forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dv_dt depends only on x (dv_dt = f(x)) with no v or t terms, the dynamics are conservative (force derived from a potential), implying energy-like invariants.
- A term -c * v indicates linear viscous damping; adding -c * Abs(v) * v indicates quadratic drag typical at higher Reynolds number motion.
- Odd restoring terms in x (e.g., -c1*x - c2*x**3) suggest a symmetric potential well about x=0; inclusion of even powers in the force (e.g., x**2) typically indicates asymmetry or bias.
- Using sin(x) for restoring force signals large-angle pendulum behavior; for small amplitudes sin(x) ≈ x recovers linear stiffness.
- A factor (1 - c * x**2) * v (Van der Pol form) implies negative damping for small |x| and positive damping for large |x|, producing a stable limit cycle (self-sustained oscillations).
- A factor (1 - c * v**2) * v (Rayleigh form) implies energy injection at small |v| and dissipation at large |v|, another route to limit cycles.
- Explicit periodic dependence on t (sin/cos terms added to dv_dt) indicates external forcing; harmonics (multiple frequencies) often model non-sinusoidal drives or coupled excitations.
- A time-periodic coefficient multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates parametric excitation; resonance bands and instability tongues are expected (Mathieu behavior).
- Cross-coupled damping like (c0 + c1*x**2)*v implies amplitude-dependent dissipation, often used to fit nonlinear friction or internal material damping.

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(x,t,v)=0.767518260471059\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.263896435020576\,v\sin(x).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to produce **(i)** a pure \(\sin(t)\) term with constant amplitude, and **(ii)** a **product** term \(v\sin(x)\) with constant coefficient, and **(iii)** no extra dependence (no constants, no pure \(v\), no \(\cos(t)\), no \(\sin(x)\) alone, no \(|v|\), etc.) after choosing parameters.

I’ll check each candidate for whether it can be reduced (by setting some parameters to 0 and using phase shifts) to exactly \(A\sin(t)+B\,v\sin(x)\).

---

### 1. `c0*v + c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c4*v*x**c5 + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)*Abs(v)**c9`

- No way to create \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

**GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v = 0.767518*sin(t) - 0.263896*v*sin(x)**

The GT has two terms:
1. A `sin(t)` term
2. A `v*sin(x)` term

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Candidate 1: c0*v + c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + c4*v*x^c5 + c6*sin(c7*t + c8)*|v|^c9

The GT needs `v*sin(x)`. This candidate has `v`, `v*x^c5`, `sin(t)*|v|^c9`, and `sin(t)`. None of these produce `v*sin(x)`. The term `v*x^c5` is a power of x, not sin(x). Cannot match.

**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*exp(c4*x)*sin(c1*t+c2) + c5*exp(c6*v)*cos(c7*t+c8)

This has sin(t) terms (possibly multiplied by exp(x)) and exp(v)*cos(t). No `v*sin(x)` term. The exp(c6*v) cannot be linearized to v. Cannot match.

**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: Same as Candidate 2 + c9*v*|v|

Has v*|v| but no v*sin(x). Cannot match.

**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: c0*v + c1*v*|v| + c2*v*|v| + c3*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6*cos(c7*t) + c8*cos(c9*t)*|v|

No v*sin(x) term. Has v, v*|v|, sin(t), cos(t), cos(t)*|v|. Setting c1=c2=0, c6=0, c8=0 gives c0*v + c3*sin(c4*t+c5). This is v (not v*sin(x)) plus sin(t). Cannot match GT which requires v*sin(x).

**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**
